<p><b>Martin Fourcade</b> (born 14 September 1988) is a French <a href="/wiki/Biathlon" title="Biathlon">biathlete</a> and <a href="/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer" title="Non-commissioned officer">non-commissioned officer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Fourcade is a ten-time <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships" title="Biathlon World Championships">World Champion</a>, twice an <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_Winter_Olympics" title="Biathlon at the Winter Olympics">Olympic champion</a> and five-time winner of the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Overall World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> He is the only male biathlete to have won the Overall World Cup five times in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>With his achievements, Fourcade is the second most successful male biathlete of all time after <a href="/wiki/Ole_Einar_Bj%C3%B8rndalen" title="Ole Einar Bjørndalen">Ole Einar Bjørndalen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Records_Men_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Records_Men-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fourcade took up biathlon in 2002 and started competing internationally in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup> following in the footsteps of his older brother <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fourcade" title="Simon Fourcade">Simon Fourcade</a>. The younger Fourcade competed for France in the 2007 and 2008 <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_Junior_World_Championships" title="Biathlon Junior World Championships">Junior World Championships</a>, winning a bronze medal in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon#Relay" title="Biathlon">relay</a> in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade first competed in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Biathlon World Cup</a> at <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> in March 2008, finishing 61st in what would be his only World Cup appearance that season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008-09_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008-09 Biathlon World Cup">next season</a> was already much more successful for him, as he grabbed his first World Cup points at <a href="/wiki/Hochfilzen" title="Hochfilzen">Hochfilzen</a>, placing 36th in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon#Individual" title="Biathlon">individual race</a> and 10th in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon#Sprint" title="Biathlon">sprint</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup> His best results that year came at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2009" title="Biathlon World Championships 2009">2009 World Championships</a>, where he finished in the top 20 in every competition, including an 8th place in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2009_%E2%80%93_12.5_km_Pursuit_Men" title="Biathlon World Championships 2009 – 12.5 km Pursuit Men">pursuit</a> and a 4th place in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Biathlon_World_Championships_2009_%E2%80%93_4_x_7.5_km_Relay_Men&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Biathlon World Championships 2009 – 4 x 7.5 km Relay Men (page does not exist)">relay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Fourcade finished 24th in the overall World Cup that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.9310_season">2009–10 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2009–10 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Fourcade again improved in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009-10_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009-10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 season</a>, consistently finishing in the top 10 and making the French team for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>, together with his brother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Fourcade grabbed a silver medal in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Men's mass start">mass start</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> marking the first time he made the podium in a World Cup event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup> Fourcade then claimed his first victory in a pursuit at <a href="/wiki/Kontiolahti" title="Kontiolahti">Kontiolahti</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and followed up with two more first places at <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, in a sprint and another pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-6"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oslopu3_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-oslopu3-16">[16]</a></sup> The two pursuit victories meant Fourcade won the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup_%E2%80%93_Pursuit_Men" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup – Pursuit Men">2009–10 Pursuit World Cup</a>, edging out <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Simon_Eder" title="Simon Eder">Simon Eder</a> by just one point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oslopu3_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-oslopu3-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In the overall World Cup he finished 5th, 64 points ahead of his brother Simon, who finished a career-best 7th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2010–11 Biathlon World Cup">2010–11 season</a> was also highly successful for Fourcade. He opened the season at <a href="/wiki/%C3%96stersund" title="Östersund">Östersund</a> with three top 5 finishes, including two 3rd places. After somewhat weaker showings at <a href="/wiki/Pokljuka" title="Pokljuka">Pokljuka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oberhof,_Germany" title="Oberhof, Germany">Oberhof</a>, Fourcade placed runner-up in all three races at <a href="/wiki/Ruhpolding" title="Ruhpolding">Ruhpolding</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-7"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Fourcade won mass starts at both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antholz" title="Antholz">Antholz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Kent,_Maine" title="Fort Kent, Maine">Fort Kent</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-8"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and entered the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011">2011 World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Khanty-Mansiysk" title="Khanty-Mansiysk">Khanty-Mansiysk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> as one of the favourites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first event at the World Championships was the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Mixed_relay" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Mixed relay">mixed relay</a>, where the French placed 3rd after Fourcade as anchor showed the best male performance in the race to lift his team up from 5th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Fourcade then claimed the silver medal behind <a href="/wiki/Arnd_Peiffer" title="Arnd Peiffer">Arnd Peiffer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Men's sprint">sprint</a>, despite missing two shots at the prone stage; Fourcade was the fastest skier in the competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The next day in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Men's pursuit">pursuit</a> Fourcade won the gold despite three penalties,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> thanks to turning in another fastest skiing performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade finished 3rd in the Overall World Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> 4th in the Sprint, 2nd in the Pursuit, 3rd in the Individual and 2nd in the Mass Start.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.9312_season">2011–12 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2011–12 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1338" data-file-width="2008" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg/280px-Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg/420px-Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg/560px-Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Fourcade_Kontiolahti_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kontiolahti" title="Kontiolahti">Kontiolahti</a>, Finland, February 12, 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fourcade had the best possible start in 2011–12 season with 2 wins in the individual<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and the pursuit<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> in Östersund, Sweden, leading the Overall ranking for the first time.</p>
<p>In Nove Mesto, Czech Republic, he finished 3rd in the sprint, alongside his older brother Simon who took the 2nd place, behind Norway's <a href="/wiki/Emil_Hegle_Svendsen" title="Emil Hegle Svendsen">Emil Hegle Svendsen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> It was the first time in biathlon's history that 2 brothers stood on a podium together. In the following pursuit (although finishing respectively 2nd and 3rd) Simon was downgraded to 4th place after IBU decided to upgrade Germany's Arnd Peiffer following a target's malfunction (Peiffer did an extra lap). But the French team claimed Martin had purposely slowed down before crossing the line, seeing that Simon was far behind. IBU finally decided to tie Peiffer and Martin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Antholz was a fantastic weekend for the French team, both men and women relays taking 1st place and Fourcade finishing 3rd of the sprint and the mass Start.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>On home soil in Oslo, Emil Hegle Svendsen grabbed the yellow bib from Fourcade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first to start, Fourcade managed to win the sprint despite extreme temperatures in Kontiolahti, Finland (−18 °C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012">World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ruhpolding" title="Ruhpolding">Ruhpolding</a>, Fourcade won three gold medals in sprint, pursuit and mass start.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> He became only the third male biathlete to win three non-team gold medals at a single World Championships after Raphaël Poirée (<a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2004" title="Biathlon World Championships 2004">Oberhof 2004</a>) and Ole Einar Bjørndalen (<a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2005" title="Biathlon World Championships 2005">Hochfilzen 2005</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2009" title="Biathlon World Championships 2009">Pyeongchang 2009</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sports_123:_Biathlon_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sports_123:_Biathlon-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade won the Overall World Cup for the first time, as well as the discipline titles in the sprint and the pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.9313_season">2012–13 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012–13 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Fourcade started the season with a win in the individual in Östersund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> At the time he had improved his shooting to 89%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Hochfilzen, Fourcade finished 2nd and 3rd in the sprint and in the pursuit, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Having had mediocre weekends in Pokljuka and Oberhof, Fourcade went on to win both the sprint and the mass start in Ruhpolding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2013" title="Biathlon World Championships 2013">World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nov%C3%A9_M%C4%9Bsto_na_Morav%C4%9B" title="Nové Město na Moravě">Nove Mesto</a>, Fourcade had to settle for silver both in sprint and in pursuit as Emil Hegle Svendsen won both events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www3.biathlonworld.com_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-www3.biathlonworld.com-46">[46]</a></sup> In the latter, Fourcade lost the gold by one tenth of a second to Svendsen, leaving the Frenchman disappointed, citing that he would "think of that 2,4 cm everyday when training next summer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www3.biathlonworld.com_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-www3.biathlonworld.com-46">[46]</a></sup> Fourcade was, however, able to take a gold in the individual, his fifth World Championships gold medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The end of the season was a successful one for Fourcade, as he picked up wins in the pursuit in Oslo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> in the individual and in the sprint in Sochi<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and in the sprint and in the mass start in Khanty-Mansiysk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www4.biathlonworld.com_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-www4.biathlonworld.com-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade finished the season with over 400 overall world cup points more than Svendsen who finished second, thus winning his second Overall World Cup title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In addition, he won all of discipline titles, becoming only the second male biathlete after Raphaël Poirée to win all of the crystal globes in one season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www4.biathlonworld.com_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-www4.biathlonworld.com-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2013.E2.80.9314_season">2013–14 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013–14 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Just like in the previous season, Fourcade started the 2013-14 season by winning the Östersund individual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In addition, he won the sprint two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> He then went on to take a third win of the season in Hochfilzen pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Fourcade couldn't, however, add to his win count in <a href="/wiki/Annecy" title="Annecy">Annecy</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, his best result being third in the sprint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3888" data-file-width="2592" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG/220px-2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG/330px-2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG/440px-2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2014-01-04_Biathlon_World_Cup_Oberhof_-_Mens_Pursuit_-_3_-_Martin_Fourcade_3.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Martin Fourcade in <a href="/wiki/Oberhof,_Germany" title="Oberhof, Germany">Oberhof</a> in January 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the start of the year 2014 Fourcade won the mass start in Oberhof, his first World Cup victory there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-58">[58]</a></sup> He then decided to skip the Ruhpolding weekend to train for the olympics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> His final tune-up for the olympics, the Antholz World Cup weekend wasn't all that successful, although the French team, anchored by Martin Fourcade, did win the men's relay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a> Fourcade admitted that he will be under pressure, but that he will be able to handle it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> He also said that he is capable of winning every race he enters but that there will be others, mainly Emil Hegle Svendsen, with a great level of self-confidence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The first non-team race, the sprint, ended in disappointing sixth place for Fourcade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> However, he was able to turn the tables in the following pursuit, climbing from sixth to first, winning his first olympic gold medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> After the last shot at the last standing shooting Fourcade famously stretched his arm in the air and pumped his fist, explaining that it was all happiness, knowing the weight of that shooting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In the individual, Fourcade carried on his good form, hitting 19 out of 20 targets in winning his second olympic gold medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The mass-start ended in a slight disappointment for Fourcade, for even though claiming his third medal of the games, a silver, he lost the gold by some centimeters, Svendsen claiming the victory in photo-finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Regardless of that, Fourcade was by far the most successful male biathlete of the 2014 Winter Olympics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In addition, he became only the second male biathlete after Ole Einar Bjørndalen to have won a non-team Olympic gold medal, a non-team World Championships gold medal, the Overall World Cup title and all of the discipline World Cup titles in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sports_123:_Biathlon_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sports_123:_Biathlon-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-real_biathlon:_Records_Men_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-real_biathlon:_Records_Men-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the olympics there were three weekends left in the world cup, with Fourcade claiming the second place in the Pokljuka mass start,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and second places in the Kontiolahti sprint and pursuit (<a href="/wiki/Johannes_Thingnes_B%C3%B8" title="Johannes Thingnes Bø">Johannes Thingnes Bø</a> winning both of the Kontiolahti races).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kontiolahtibiathlon.com_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-kontiolahtibiathlon.com-73">[73]</a></sup> With the pursuit second place, Fourcade secured his third Overall World Cup title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kontiolahtibiathlon.com_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-kontiolahtibiathlon.com-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade won the final event of the season, the Oslo mass start, which ensured that he won the mass start crystal globe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> He finished the season with the Overall crystal globe as well as sprint, pursuit and mass start crystal globes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014.E2.80.9315_season">2014–15 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2014–15 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before the season Fourcade suffered from <a href="/wiki/Infectious_mononucleosis" title="Infectious mononucleosis">mononucleosis</a> and was forced to heavily cut back his training hours in the summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike the two previous years, Fourcade couldn't win the Östersund individual, in fact with six shooting errors he slumped to 81st place, his second worst World Cup result ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> This appeared to be only temporary, however, as he won both of the following races, the sprint and the pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>His next victory came in the Hochfilzen pursuit where he climbed from seventh place to first, thanks to a clean shooting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Pokljuka was not as successful, as Fourcade didn't add to his win tally. Even so, he collected second most points of the weekend behind <a href="/wiki/Anton_Shipulin" title="Anton Shipulin">Anton Shipulin</a> of Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Oberhof weekend at the start of the year 2015 was a very successful one for the French star as he won both the sprint and the mass start.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The final shooting of the mass start was one of the most memorable moments of the season as a strong wind forced the leading Fourcade to wait patiently for it to calm down while many athletes, including eventual runner-up Anton Shipulin, left the shooting range. None of them shot clean, however, and it was the clean shooting Fourcade who again took the lead and the victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>After two below par -weekends, when Shipulin and most notably <a href="/wiki/Simon_Schempp" title="Simon Schempp">Simon Schempp</a> of Germany were able to reduce the gap to Fourcade in the Overall World Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> the Frenchman was able to regroup to score fourth and third places in Nove Mesto sprint and pursuit, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The last weekend before the world championships, the Oslo weekend, saw Fourcade complete the return to form, as the Frenchman won the individual race. He started first, shot 20 out of 20 and stayed on top until the end.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Fourcade then went on to take the second place behind Arnd Peiffer in the sprint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2015" title="Biathlon World Championships 2015">World Championships</a> in Kontiolahti, Fourcade didn't medal in the three other non-team events, but won his sixth world championships gold medal in the individual. Having made one shooting error on the second prone stage he had to play catch up, as his rival Emil Hegle Svendsen had cleared all the targets earlier. Fourcade didn't make any more shooting mistakes and overtook Svendsen at the finish to take the gold. If it hadn't been for the late success of eventual bronze medalist <a href="/wiki/Ond%C5%99ej_Moravec" title="Ondřej Moravec">Ondrej Moravec</a>, the elder of the Fourcade brothers, Simon, would have been on the podium as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> By claiming his sixth non-team gold, Martin Fourcade became the third most successful non-team gold medal winning male biathlete at the World Championships after Ole Einar Bjørndalen and Raphaël Poirée, moving ahead of his rival Svendsen, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aleksander_Tikhonov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aleksander Tikhonov (page does not exist)">Aleksander Tikhonov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ullrich" title="Frank Ullrich">Frank Ullrich</a> who have five non-team gold medals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-real_biathlon:_Records_Men_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-real_biathlon:_Records_Men-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the season finale in Khanty-Mansiysk, Fourcade claimed a victory in the sprint, his 8th win of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> He then finished 4th in the pursuit, which was enough to secure the big crystal globe, as well as the pursuit discipline title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the off season mononucleosis, Fourcade finished the season winning the Overall World Cup title and the sprint and pursuit discipline titles. He became the first male biathlete to win the Overall title four times in succession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2015.E2.80.9316_season">2015–16 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2015–16 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before starting his biathlon campaign for 2015-16, Fourcade had a brief foray into cross-country skiing, finishing 12th in a 15 km freestyle FIS race at <a href="/wiki/Beitost%C3%B8len" title="Beitostølen">Beitostølen</a> before competing in the opening meeting of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_FIS_Cross-Country_World_Cup" title="2015–16 FIS Cross-Country World Cup">2015–16 FIS Cross-Country World Cup</a> at <a href="/wiki/Rukatunturi" title="Rukatunturi">Ruka</a>, where he finished 22nd in the 10 km freestyle, posting the third best French performance of the day, and beating his previous personal best result on the Cross-Country World Cup of a 47th place in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like the year before, Fourcade started the season with an indifferent showing in the Östersund individual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> And like the previous year, he was able to regroup to win both of the two other solo Östersund races, the sprint and the pursuit. He missed five times in the two competitions altogether, but was still able to win both races quite comfortably with his outstanding ski speed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Hochfilzen, Fourcade and Simon Schempp dominated the field, with Schempp winning the sprint and Fourcade finishing second and the two swapping places in the following pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The Pokljuka weekend was a good but not a great one for Fourcade, as he collected third most world cup points there. Schempp was, however, able to gain on the lead of Fourcade quite considerably.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>With world number two Bjørndalen and world number three Schempp absent from the first two and all three Oberhof-replacing Ruhpolding races, respectively, Fourcade was able to take a sizeable lead in the overall rankings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> After the first of the two Ruhpolding weekends, a familiar threat in Emil Hegle Svendsen took over as the nearest challenger to Fourcade in the overall rankings. However, Fourcade was able to take a big lead in the final race of the weekend, the mass start. The two great rivals arrived toe to toe at the final standing shoot, only for Fourcade to hit all five targets and win the race and Svendsen to miss three times and fall to the 13th place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade then carried on the good form by winning the Ruhpolding individual race and placing second in the mass start.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The next weekend, the Antholz weekend was a poor one for Fourcade, although he did rise from 28th place to fourth in the pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The trip to North America started very well for Fourcade, as he won the Canmore sprint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> He also took the Canmore single mixed relay with <a href="/wiki/Marie_Dorin_Habert" title="Marie Dorin Habert">Marie Dorin Habert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In the Presque Isle sprint, Fourcade finished third behind Johannes Thingnes Bø and Anton Shipulin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> In the following pursuit, Bø seemed to be on his way to winning a double before missing twice on the last shooting. Fourcade, some 40 seconds back, cleared all five targets and left the range before his Norwegian rival. By claiming the pursuit, Fourcade equalled the number of world cup race wins of Raphaël Poirée, with 44 victories. The race also marked the 100th time Fourcade wore the prestigious yellow bib.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>To prepare for the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2016" title="Biathlon World Championships 2016">2016 World Championships</a> in Oslo, Fourcade had bought an apartment in Oslo with the help of his friend, <a href="/wiki/Tarjei_B%C3%B8" title="Tarjei Bø">Tarjei Bø</a> in June 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Judging by his success in the championships, this seemed to be a good move. Fourcade started by anchoring the French mixed relay team to gold medal<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> before winning both the sprint and the pursuit in convincing fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-118">[118]</a></sup> With these gold medals, Fourcade secured his fifth straight Overall World Cup title and brought his number of World Championships gold medals to nine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-118">[118]</a></sup> He then went on to keep the golden streak going by winning the individual race. Fourcade had a one-minute penalty at the first standing stage but like the three previous major individual races, the one mistake proved to be his only one. That turned out to be just enough to beat clean shooting <a href="/wiki/Dominik_Landertinger" title="Dominik Landertinger">Dominik Landertinger</a> of Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> By claiming his tenth World Championship gold medal and ninth non-team gold medal, Fourcade became the first biathlete ever to win the longest event in biathlon three times in succession at the World Championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> In addition, Fourcade claimed the individual discipline crystal globe with a margin of two points over bronze medallist Simon Eder of Austria, leaving the great Frenchman all but certain to win all of the crystal globes that season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> The final race of the championships, the mass start, saw Fourcade narrowly miss the chance to win all four non-team gold medals as Johannes Thingnes Bø edged the Frenchman on the last loop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> With his non-team medals, Fourcade became only the second male biathlete to win three golds and one silver in non-team competitions in a single World Championships, after Raphaël Poirée (Oberhof 2004). And by claiming three non-team gold medals to take his career tally to 9, Fourcade became the second most successful non-team gold medal winning male biathlete at the World Championships after Ole Einar Bjørndalen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Records_Men_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Records_Men-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade finished the season winning the overall World Cup title as well as all of the discipline titles, becoming the first male biathlete to win all five crystal globes of a season multiple times. The overall title was his fifth in succession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016.E2.80.9317_season">2016–17 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2016–17 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Yet again the first competition weekend of the season in Östersund proved to be a successful one for Fourcade. He started the campaign with a convincing victory in the mixed relay with Marie Dorin Habert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Fourcade then won the individual race, the first non-team race of the season, despite two missed shots at the first standing stage. He hit all the remaining targets while Johannes Thingnes Bø, who had a comfortable lead coming to the last shooting, fell victim to nerves and a strong wind and missed two targets. This allowed fast-skiing Fourcade to take the victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The sprint was a dominant race for Fourcade, who missed no targets and outskied everyone else.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Fourcade couldn't, however, complete the Östersund clean sweep, as he surprisingly let go a 42 second lead in the pursuit. He suffered from a combination of nerves and wind to miss four targets altogether as he was beaten by the surprise pair of the season, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Babikov" title="Anton Babikov">Anton Babikov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Tsvetkov" title="Maxim Tsvetkov">Maxim Tsvetkov</a> of Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> The third place ensured, however, that Fourcade would take a sizeable lead in the world cup total points from the first weekend.</p>
<p>Fourcade continued his domination in Pokljuka, winning all three competitions of the weekend. He overtook a fellow clean-shooter Johannes Thingnes Bø in the sprint with a strong last loop. This ensured that Fourcade now had at least one victory at every World Cup venue in the current calendar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In the pursuit, Fourcade shot clean all stages and left Anton Shipulin, who had arrived at the last standing just after Fourcade, third behind Emil Hegle Svendsen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Fourcade then anchored the French team to victory in the relay, having had a 20 second head start thanks to three good legs from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Guillaume_Beatrix" title="Jean Guillaume Beatrix">Jean Guillaume Beatrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Fillon_Maillet" title="Quentin Fillon Maillet">Quentin Fillon Maillet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Desthieux" title="Simon Desthieux">Simon Desthieux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the second weekend in a row, Fourcade won all three competitions of the weekend, this time in Nové Město. He won the sprint with a margin of 1,6 seconds with one penalty, outskiing the clean-shooting Anton Shipulin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Fourcade then shot a singe penalty in a convincing pursuit victory <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> and wrapped up the weekend with another 19 out of 20 targets -mass start competition, claiming his 7th non-team victory of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> By winning 7 of the 8 non-team competitions, placing third in the remaining one and winning both relay competitions, Fourcade had the most successful December in biathlon history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first race after the Christmas break was the Oberhof sprint, where Fourcade had the lead coming to the second shooting, but couldn't manage the tough winds and missed three targets. He finished eighth, his worst result of the season, thus ending the streak of 10 podium finishes and 8 non-team podium finishes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> However, Fourcade was able to turn the tables in the following pursuit. He hit 19 out of 20 targets in difficult conditions and climbed from 51 seconds back of <a href="/wiki/Julian_Eberhard" title="Julian Eberhard">Julian Eberhard</a> to win with a margin of over a minute to Arnd Peiffer. With this win, Fourcade secured having at least one victory from every competition weekend of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> In the mass start, Fourcade missed twice and finished third behind Germans Simon Schempp and Erik Lesser, despite leading after the last shooting. This was the 10th podium out of 11 races of the season for Fourcade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fourcade continued to amass victories and World Cup lead in Ruhpolding. He outskied Julian Eberhard and Emil Hegle Svendsen in the sprint, all three of them shooting clean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In the following pursuit, Eberhard dropped out of the fight for victory earlier on, but Svendsen got close to Fourcade. This was because the Frenchman missed three times in the second and third shooting combined. Before the last shooting, Svendsen had the lead for a moment and a number of other athletes caught them as well. But from there on, Fourcade opened up a lead, held his nerve and technique to shoot clean, and easily held his lead in the final lap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Competition weekend number 6 in Antholtz in the typically challenging venue for Fourcade again proved to be just that. He finished second in the individual, behind Anton Shipulin, shooting two mistakes as the Russian only shot one. This was podium number 13 out of 14 non-team competitions for Fourcade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> He then skipped the relay to prepare for the mass start. He couldn't, however, reach the podium this time as three missed shots left him fifth, thus ending his five-weekend streak of at least one victory and at least one non-team victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Achievements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All statistics are sourced from the <a href="/wiki/International_Biathlon_Union" title="International Biathlon Union">International Biathlon Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-9"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Cup">World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>5 overall World Cup titles (2nd to Ole Einar Bjørndalen, 6 titles)</li>
<li>5 overall World Cup titles in a row (all-time record)</li>
<li>16 discipline World Cup titles (2nd to Bjørndalen, 20 titles)</li>
<li>2 times the clean sweep of all five crystal globes won in one season (all-time record)</li>
<li>57 non-team World Cup victories (2nd to Bjørndalen, 94 victories)</li>
<li>10 non-team World Cup victories in one season (3rd behind Bjørndalen and Raphaël Poirée, 12 and 11 victories respectively)</li>
<li>57 non-team World Cup victories out of 203 non-team starts, 28.1% win rate (all-time record)</li>
<li>103 non-team World Cup podiums out of 203 non-team starts, 50.7% podium rate (all-time record)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Games">Olympic Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Olympic Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>2 gold medals and 2 silver medals (11th on all-time list)</li>
<li>2 non-team gold medals and 2 non-team silver medals (2nd to Bjørndalen, 5 gold medals, 3 silver medals and 1 bronze medal)</li>
<li>2 non-team gold medals and 1 non-team silver medal in a single Olympic Games (2nd to Bjørndalen, 3 gold medals)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Championships">World Championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: World Championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>10 gold medals, 8 silver medals and 2 bronze medals (5th on all-time list)</li>
<li>9 non-team gold medals and 4 non-team silver medals (2nd to Bjørndalen, 11 gold medals, 6 silver medals and 8 bronze medals)</li>
<li>3 non-team gold medals and 1 non-team silver medal in a single World Championships (all-time record shared with Poirée)</li>
<li>5 World Championships in a row with at least 1 non-team gold medal (all-time record shared with Frank Ullrich)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_2">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>6 Major Championships (Olympic Games and World Championships) in a row with at least 1 non-team gold medal (all-time record shared with Ullrich)</li>
<li>2 times the winner of a "Grand Slam" of a non-team olympic gold medal, a non-team World Championships gold medal, the overall World Cup title and all of the discipline World Cup titles (all-time record)</li>
<li>6 years in row with at least 7 World Cup or Olympic Games non-team victories (all-time record)</li>
<li>59 World Cup and Olympic Games non-team victories (2nd to Bjørndalen, 95 victories)</li>
<li>69 World Cup and Olympic Games victories altogether (2nd to Bjørndalen, 132 victories)</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Martin Fourcade was born in <a href="/wiki/Perpignan" title="Perpignan">Perpignan, France</a> on 14 September 1988 to Gisèle and Marcel Fourcade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>He has a daughter, Manon (born on 11 September 2015), with his partner Hélène.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biathlon_results">Biathlon results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Biathlon results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>All results are sourced from the <a href="/wiki/International_Biathlon_Union" title="International Biathlon Union">International Biathlon Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibuprofile_7-10"><a href="#cite_note-ibuprofile-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Games_2">Olympic Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Fourcade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Olympic Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>4 medals (2 gold, 2 silver)</i></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">
<tr>
